## 1) Tech Spec — V1

Markdown

```
# Tech Spec — Promptr V1## Stack- Frontend: Next.js App Router + TypeScript + Tailwind- UI: shadcn/ui + Lucide icons + Framer Motion- Fonts: Red Hat Display + Red Hat Mono- Backend: Next.js API routes / server actions- LLM: OpenAI Responses API- Model: `gpt-5.2`- Database: Supabase Postgres- File parsing:  - txt: native text read  - md: native text read  - docx: mammoth- PDF export: html2pdf or pdf-lib- Deployment: Vercel- Repo: GitHub## Why This Stack- fast enough for hackathon- clean Vercel deploy path- external DB works with serverless- polished SPA possible without overengineering- OpenAI `gpt-5.2` tested as strongest production model for Promptr V1## App ArchitectureFrontend SPA→ user submits prompt→ `/api/transform`→ OpenAI Responses API + Promptr system prompt→ structured 4-panel JSON response→ UI renders panel flow→ session + outputs saved to Supabase## LLM Behavior ContractThe model must return:- panel_1_activation_prompt- panel_2_change_summary- panel_3_machine_layer- panel_4_next_steps- classification- framework_used- assumptions_if_any## Recommended OpenAI Call Shape- endpoint: Responses API- model: `gpt-5.2`- reasoning: `medium`- temperature: low / default stable- output format: structured JSON## Supabase Tables### 1. sessionsTracks every user attempt.Columns:- id (uuid, pk)- session_token (text, unique)- first_name (text, nullable)- email (text, nullable)- source (text, default 'web')- status (text)   - started  - submitted  - generated  - completed  - abandoned- created_at (timestamptz)- updated_at (timestamptz)- completed_at (timestamptz, nullable)### 2. prompt_inputsStores original prompt payload.Columns:- id (uuid, pk)- session_id (uuid, fk -> sessions.id)- input_type (text)  - paste  - txt  - md  - docx- file_name (text, nullable)- raw_prompt (text)- normalized_prompt (text, nullable)- created_at (timestamptz)### 3. prompt_outputsStores transformed results.Columns:- id (uuid, pk)- session_id (uuid, fk -> sessions.id)- classification (text)- framework_used (text)- panel_1_activation_prompt (text)- panel_2_change_summary (jsonb)- panel_3_machine_layer (text)- panel_4_next_steps (text)- assumptions (text, nullable)- model_name (text)- reasoning_level (text)- created_at (timestamptz)### 4. panel_eventsTracks progress through the flow.Columns:- id (uuid, pk)- session_id (uuid, fk -> sessions.id)- panel_name (text)  - intro  - input  - loading  - panel_1  - panel_2  - panel_3  - panel_4- event_type (text)  - viewed  - advanced  - backed  - copied  - downloaded_txt  - downloaded_md  - downloaded_pdf  - email_opened  - email_submitted- event_value (text, nullable)- created_at (timestamptz)### 5. launch_interestOptional separate capture table for cleaner email handling.Columns:- id (uuid, pk)- session_id (uuid, fk -> sessions.id)- email (text)- created_at (timestamptz)## Naming Conventions- snake_case in DB- camelCase in app code- explicit panel naming, no magic strings buried everywhere- shared types in `/lib/types.ts`## API Routes### POST `/api/transform`Input:- sessionToken- firstName?- rawPrompt- inputType- fileName?Output:- classification- frameworkUsed- panel1- panel2- panel3- panel4### POST `/api/session/start`Creates or resumes anonymous session.### POST `/api/session/email`Stores optional email.### POST `/api/events`Stores analytics events.## Validation Rules- minimum prompt length: 40 chars- max prompt length: reasonable safe cap for demo- accepted files only: `.txt`, `.md`, `.docx`- reject empty or unreadable uploads gracefully- sanitize all input before storage## UI States- intro- input- loading- results_panel_1- results_panel_2- results_panel_3- results_panel_4- done## Visual Specs- background: #050505- card: #0f0f0f / glass- text: #fafafa- muted text: #9da4af- restrained bright accents:  - #9b5cff  - #2de2e6  - #ff2f92  - optional #f97316- left-aligned content inside centered container- ~70% width desktop- 75–80% max width mobile- Apple-site sleekness, subtle motion only## Performance Notes- keep first transform call as single request- do not chain multiple models in V1- avoid over-animated clutter- defer heavy PDF styling until output exists## Security / Privacy- no auth required- anonymous session token only- never expose API keys client-side- server-only OpenAI call- sanitize uploads- clear privacy note near input if needed## Observability / GTM MetricsTrack:- session starts- prompt submitted- input type- classification- framework chosen- panel views- panel drop-off- copy events- download events- email open- email submit- completion rate## V2 Notes- compare framework reruns- support screenshots / PDF / URLs- support 3-model showdown- support saved prompt library- support inline edits
```

## 4) Promptr agent logic / guardrails file

TypeScript

```
// prompts/promptr-v1-system.tsexport const PROMPTR_V1_SYSTEM_PROMPT = `You are Promptr V1, an ND Prompt Refactor Architect.Your job:Transform an overwhelming, multipart, abandonment-prone prompt into a two-layer output system:1) a human-safe ND-friendly activation prompt2) a machine-safe backend prompt for stronger LLM executionAlso explain what changed and give the smallest next step so the user can actually use it.Core goal:Reduce cognitive overload without weakening strategic quality.Success criteria:- The user can understand and use the rewritten prompt without freezing.- The machine-layer prompt is stronger than the original.- The output is visibly better than the input.- The response feels sharp, useful, and human.Voice:- direct- smart- slightly rebellious- punchy- crisp- not corporate- not clinical- not motivational- not paddedHard style rules:- Do not use em dashes.- Do not over-explain.- Do not write long walls of text.- Do not sound like a therapist, professor, or generic copywriter.- Prefer short sections and crisp labels.- Prioritize clarity over cleverness.- Use sentence fragments when they hit harder.- Do not make the output more boring than the input.Assumptions:- The input may be messy, contradictory, incomplete, or emotionally overloaded.- Do not reject messy input.- Do not require perfect structure.- If needed, infer the most likely intent and proceed.- If a critical detail is missing, mention the assumption briefly in Panel 2.- Ask a clarifying question only if the prompt is impossible to salvage without it. If so, ask exactly one question and stop.Classify the prompt silently first into one of these:- writing- profile_or_bio- offer_or_sales- workflow_or_system- planning_or_strategy- agent_or_app_builder- intake_or_audit- mixed_or_otherFramework selection:Choose one primary framework only.Frameworks:- FOG = Friction -> Outcome -> GuardrailUse when the prompt is sprawling, undefined, or too broad.- MVP = Minimum Viable PermissionUse when perfectionism, fear, shame, or resistance is blocking action.- SNAP = State -> Next step -> Authority -> ProofUse when the user sounds stuck, flooded, avoidant, or needs a single next move.- PACE = Permission -> Anchor -> Containment -> ExecutionUse when both strategic complexity and cognitive overload are present.Default to PACE when multiple issues are present.Transformation rules:- Do not simply summarize the original prompt.- Do not lightly rewrite it and call it done.- Extract the actual task, desired outcome, hidden friction, and execution blockers.- Separate human friction from machine logic.- Turn blank-filling complexity into a smaller entry move.- Reduce decisions where possible.- Preserve strategic nuance where it matters.- Remove theatrics that do not improve output quality.- Keep enough specificity so the rewritten prompt still works.Output contract:Return valid JSON with exactly these keys:{  "classification": string,  "frameworkUsed": string,  "assumptions": string | null,  "panel1ActivationPrompt": string,  "panel2WhatChanged": {    "frameworkUsed": string,    "cut": string,    "clarified": string,    "rebuilt": string,    "whyItWorksBetter": string  },  "panel3MachineLayer": string,  "panel4UseThisNext": string}Panel requirements:Panel 1:- Human-usable version first- Easier to start- Less overwhelming- One clear path- Copy/paste readyPanel 2:- Brief- Blunt- Satisfying- Mention assumptions only if neededPanel 3:- Strong backend prompt- Clear role- Clear task- Constraints- Output format- Guardrails- Stronger than the originalPanel 4:- Tell the user to copy the ND-safe version first- Tell them to run it in their preferred LLM or agent- Mention they can save the bot-speak spec to build their own agent- Give one strongest next step only- Keep it shortGuardrails:- Do not shame the user.- Do not say the original prompt is bad.- Do not tell the user to calm down or try harder.- Do not replace sharp brand voice with generic professionalism.- Do not add fake specificity.- Do not over-compress so hard that the machine layer loses teeth.- If the prompt is clearly for a lead magnet, agent, or app, keep the output productizable.Final instruction:Extract the signal.Externalize the chaos.Make the damn thing usable.`.trim();
```

# Promptr V1 test steps — before final production DB## GoalValidate:- model quality- JSON output shape- panel usefulness- file parsing- flow integrityDo this before you fully wire the production database.---## Step 1 — Local envCreate `.env.local`Required:- OPENAI_API_KEY=- NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL=- NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY=- SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY=If you are not ready to wire Supabase yet, stub session storage in memory for first-pass UI tests.---## Step 2 — First backend smoke testBuild `/api/transform` first.Use a hardcoded local test prompt in terminal or Postman:- one ugly LinkedIn optimizer mega-prompt- one app builder mega-prompt- one writing / offer mega-promptSuccess =- valid JSON- all 4 panels populated- framework selected- assumptions null or brief- no markdown wrapper around JSON---## Step 3 — Test prompt builderVerify the backend is actually injecting:- system prompt- user prompt- structured response instructionsFailure signs:- model returns prose essay- malformed JSON- missing panel keys- panel 1 and panel 3 too similar---## Step 4 — Terminal test commandUse curl or your Antigravity terminal runner.Example:\`\`\`bashcurl -X POST http://localhost:3000/api/transform \\  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \\  -d '{    "sessionToken": "test-session-001",    "rawPrompt": "PASTE A REAL MESSY PROMPT HERE",    "inputType": "paste"  }'\`\`\`Inspect:- classification- frameworkUsed- panel1ActivationPrompt- panel3MachineLayer---## Step 5 — Quality test rubricFor each result, check:### Panel 1- Is it actually easier to use?- Did it reduce overwhelm?- Would an ND founder use this?### Panel 2- Is it short and sharp?- Does it explain the transformation without rambling?### Panel 3- Is it stronger than the original?- Does it preserve the strategic bones?- Is it clearly machine-oriented?### Panel 4- Is the next move obvious?- Is it short enough to act on immediately?---## Step 6 — File parsing testsTest:- .txt- .md- .docxVerify:- prompt text extracts cleanly- formatting junk is stripped- unreadable files fail gracefully---## Step 7 — UI flow testsCheck:- intro screen- input screen- loading screen- panel flow- back / next- machine layer collapse toggle- export actions- launch curious toggleFailure signs:- too much clutter- jittery motion- too much text on one screen- weak contrast- step confusion---## Step 8 — Event logging stubBefore full DB wiring, at least console-log:- session start- submit- panel view- panel advance- copy- download- email submitThen replace with Supabase inserts.---## Step 9 — Supabase wire-upAfter transform and UI are stable:- create schema- wire session creation- wire prompt input save- wire output save- wire panel events- wire email captureDo not do this before the transform route works.---## Step 10 — Fallback model testKeep one env var fallback:- OPENAI_MODEL=gpt-5.2- fallback option = gpt-5If latency or cost gets ugly, switch and compare.---## Step 11 — Final demo checklistBefore deploying:- no broken JSON- no empty panel states- uploads work- exports work- email capture works- machine layer toggle works- no ugly default Tailwind colors- no placeholder copy left behind
```

## 1) Rewritten tech spec — Astro/Vite version

Markdown

```
# Tech Spec — Promptr V1 (Astro Version)## Stack- Frontend shell: Astro- Interactive UI: React islands inside Astro- Build tool: Vite (via Astro)- Language: TypeScript- Styling: Tailwind CSS- UI primitives: custom components + Lucide icons + Framer Motion- Fonts: Red Hat Display + Red Hat Mono- Backend: Astro server endpoints- LLM: OpenAI Responses API- Model: gpt-5.2- Database: Supabase Postgres- File parsing:  - txt: native text read  - md: native text read  - docx: mammoth- PDF export: client-side html-to-pdf or pdf-lib- Deployment: Vercel- Repo: GitHub## Why this stack- Matches your preferred build lane- Astro keeps the shell lean and fast- React islands give you just enough interactivity for:  - loading screen animation  - panel state  - upload UI  - copy/export actions  - email toggle reveal- Astro server endpoints are enough for a hackathon-grade API layer- Clean Vercel deployment path for Astro apps## Rendering mode- Astro project should run in server mode for runtime API access- API endpoints live under `src/pages/api/*`- Interactive screens should be React components loaded as client islands## Core app flowAstro page shell→ React island for app state→ user submits prompt/file→ Astro API endpoint `/api/transform`→ OpenAI Responses API→ structured 4-panel JSON→ React island renders panel-by-panel→ events + results saved to Supabase## LLM behavior contractThe model must return:- classification- frameworkUsed- assumptions- panel1ActivationPrompt- panel2WhatChanged- panel3MachineLayer- panel4UseThisNext## OpenAI config- endpoint: Responses API- model: gpt-5.2- reasoning: medium- structured JSON output required## Supabase tables### sessions- id (uuid, pk)- session_token (text, unique)- first_name (text, nullable)- email (text, nullable)- status (text)- source (text, default 'web')- created_at (timestamptz)- updated_at (timestamptz)- completed_at (timestamptz, nullable)### prompt_inputs- id (uuid, pk)- session_id (uuid, fk)- input_type (text)- file_name (text, nullable)- raw_prompt (text)- normalized_prompt (text, nullable)- created_at (timestamptz)### prompt_outputs- id (uuid, pk)- session_id (uuid, fk)- classification (text)- framework_used (text)- panel_1_activation_prompt (text)- panel_2_change_summary (jsonb)- panel_3_machine_layer (text)- panel_4_next_steps (text)- assumptions (text, nullable)- model_name (text)- reasoning_level (text)- created_at (timestamptz)### panel_events- id (uuid, pk)- session_id (uuid, fk)- panel_name (text)- event_type (text)- event_value (text, nullable)- created_at (timestamptz)### launch_interest- id (uuid, pk)- session_id (uuid, fk)- email (text)- created_at (timestamptz)## Naming conventions- DB: snake_case- app code: camelCase- shared types in `src/lib/types.ts`## API endpoints### POST `/api/session/start`Create anonymous session### POST `/api/transform`Send prompt to OpenAI, save result, return structured 4-panel payload### POST `/api/events`Track panel views, copies, downloads, progression### POST `/api/session/email`Store optional launch email## Validation- min prompt length- accepted files: .txt, .md, .docx- reject empty uploads cleanly- sanitize input before persistence## UI states- intro- input- loading- panel_1- panel_2- panel_3- panel_4## Visual system- background: #050505- card: #0f0f0f / glass- text: #fafafa- muted: #9da4af- restrained brights:  - #9b5cff  - #2de2e6  - #ff2f92  - optional #f97316- left-aligned content inside centered containers- ~70% width desktop- ~75–80% width mobile- Apple-site feel with subtle motion and glow## Non-goals for V1- no auth- no multi-model picker- no inline output editing- no OCR / image / PDF input- no public URL scraping- no side-by-side compare mode
```

## 5) One correction to the model choice wording

For the app itself, keep this:

*   **Production model:** `gpt-5.2`
    
*   **Fallback env var:** `gpt-5`
    

Because `gpt-5.2` is the flagship for coding/agentic tasks and supports structured outputs + configurable reasoning effort.   [OpenAI Platform](https://platform.openai.com/docs/models/gpt-5.2/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## Rewritten `promptr-v1-system.js`

JavaScript

```
// src/prompts/promptr-v1-system.jsexport const PROMPTR_V1_SYSTEM_PROMPT = `You are Promptr V1, an ND Prompt Refactor Architect.Your job:Transform an overwhelming, multipart, abandonment-prone prompt into a two-layer output system:1) a human-safe ND-friendly activation prompt2) a machine-safe backend prompt for stronger LLM executionAlso explain what changed and give the smallest next step so the user can actually use it.Core goal:Reduce cognitive overload without weakening strategic quality.Success criteria:- The user can understand and use the rewritten prompt without freezing.- The machine-layer prompt is stronger than the original.- The output is visibly better than the input.- The response feels sharp, useful, and human.Voice:- direct- smart- slightly rebellious- punchy- crisp- not corporate- not clinical- not motivational- not paddedHard style rules:- Do not use em dashes.- Do not over-explain.- Do not write long walls of text.- Do not sound like a therapist, professor, or generic copywriter.- Prefer short sections and crisp labels.- Prioritize clarity over cleverness.- Use sentence fragments when they hit harder.- Do not make the output more boring than the input.Assumptions:- The input may be messy, contradictory, incomplete, or emotionally overloaded.- Do not reject messy input.- Do not require perfect structure.- If needed, infer the most likely intent and proceed.- If a critical detail is missing, mention the assumption briefly in Panel 2.- Ask a clarifying question only if the prompt is impossible to salvage without it. If so, ask exactly one question and stop.Classify the prompt silently first into one of these:- writing- profile_or_bio- offer_or_sales- workflow_or_system- planning_or_strategy- agent_or_app_builder- intake_or_audit- mixed_or_otherFramework selection:Choose one primary framework only.Frameworks:- FOG = Friction -> Outcome -> GuardrailUse when the prompt is sprawling, undefined, or too broad.- MVP = Minimum Viable PermissionUse when perfectionism, fear, shame, or resistance is blocking action.- SNAP = State -> Next step -> Authority -> ProofUse when the user sounds stuck, flooded, avoidant, or needs a single next move.- PACE = Permission -> Anchor -> Containment -> ExecutionUse when both strategic complexity and cognitive overload are present.Default to PACE when multiple issues are present.Transformation rules:- Do not simply summarize the original prompt.- Do not lightly rewrite it and call it done.- Extract the actual task, desired outcome, hidden friction, and execution blockers.- Separate human friction from machine logic.- Turn blank-filling complexity into a smaller entry move.- Reduce decisions where possible.- Preserve strategic nuance where it matters.- Remove theatrics that do not improve output quality.- Keep enough specificity so the rewritten prompt still works.Output contract:Return valid JSON with exactly these keys:{  "classification": string,  "frameworkUsed": string,  "assumptions": string | null,  "panel1ActivationPrompt": string,  "panel2WhatChanged": {    "frameworkUsed": string,    "cut": string,    "clarified": string,    "rebuilt": string,    "whyItWorksBetter": string  },  "panel3MachineLayer": string,  "panel4UseThisNext": string}Panel requirements:Panel 1:- Human-usable version first- Easier to start- Less overwhelming- One clear path- Copy/paste readyPanel 2:- Brief- Blunt- Satisfying- Mention assumptions only if neededPanel 3:- Strong backend prompt- Clear role- Clear task- Constraints- Output format- Guardrails- Stronger than the originalPanel 4:- Tell the user to copy the ND-safe version first- Tell them to run it in their preferred LLM or agent- Mention they can save the bot-speak spec to build their own agent- Give one strongest next step only- Keep it shortGuardrails:- Do not shame the user.- Do not say the original prompt is bad.- Do not tell the user to calm down or try harder.- Do not replace sharp brand voice with generic professionalism.- Do not add fake specificity.- Do not over-compress so hard that the machine layer loses teeth.- If the prompt is clearly for a lead magnet, agent, or app, keep the output productizable.Final instruction:Extract the signal.Externalize the chaos.Make the damn thing usable.`.trim();
```

## Important nuance

**Astro + Vite does not force TypeScript.**  
But Astro projects often still use `.ts` files because it’s convenient.

So the rule is simple:

*   if you want **plain JS only**, I should rewrite the backend files the same way
    
*   if you’re okay with **Astro app in JS + a few TS utility files**, we can mix
    

Since you’re in a hurry, the smartest thing is: **pick one and stay consistent.**

My recommendation for speed:

*   **plain JS for everything except config defaults if needed**
    

If you want, next I’ll rewrite the **file tree** and the **Astro API starter files** in **plain JS syntax only** so Antigravity doesn’t drift.

# PRD — Promptr V1## ProductPromptr## V1 JobUser pastes or uploads one ugly mega-prompt.Promptr returns:1. ND-safe activation prompt2. What changed + why3. Machine-layer / bot-speak spec4. Use-this-next action panel## V1 Success CriteriaIf it can take one ugly mega-prompt and turn it into:- usable for an ND human- structurally strong for an LLM- visibly better than the inputthen it works.## Core UserA smart, capable, overwhelmed person who:- abandons prompts because they are too hard to fill out- freezes when a prompt is too long, too abstract, or too demanding- wants the strategic value of a strong prompt without the cognitive tax## Core ProblemMany prompts are strategically solid but neurologically hostile.Users abandon them.Or they use them badly.Or they get outputs they never act on.## Core PromisePromptr extracts the signal, externalizes the chaos, and turns it into something the user can actually use.## V1 Scope### Must Have- Intro screen- Prompt input via paste or upload- File support: .txt, .md, .docx- Anonymous session creation- Automatic prompt classification- Automatic framework selection:  - FOG  - MVP  - SNAP  - PACE- OpenAI gpt-5.2 transformation- 4-panel output flow- Copy to clipboard- Download as TXT / MD / PDF- Optional first name at start- Optional email capture at end- Save every session automatically- Track panel progression and drop-off### Nice to Have if Time- Better PDF formatting- Session restore on refresh- More polished loading phrase queue- Better empty/error states### Explicit Non-Goals for V1- No auth- No public model picker- No prompt editing between panels- No screenshots- No OCR- No PDF input- No public URL scraping- No framework compare mode- No CustomGPT builder- No SPA generator## User Flow1. Optional email capture## UX Rules- One dominant idea per screen- No walls of text- No visual clutter- No visible step counter- No visible loading bar- Left-aligned content inside centered container- Premium dark UI- Fast, obvious next move## V2 NotesPromptr V2 can:- let users rerun the same prompt through different frameworks- compare outputs side-by-side- save favorite version- support screenshots / PDFs / public URLs- turn a tested ND-ified prompt into:  - CustomGPT config  - SPA / lead magnet scaffold- allow 3-model faceoff mode- allow inline editing of outputs- support richer analytics and GTM reporting

## 1 — Tech Spec

Markdown

```
# Tech Spec — Promptr V1## Stack- Frontend shell: Astro- Interactive UI: React islands- Language: JavaScript + JSX- Styling: Tailwind CSS- Motion: Framer Motion- Icons: Lucide- Backend: Astro API endpoints- Database: Supabase Postgres- LLM: OpenAI Responses API- Model: gpt-5.2- Deployment: Vercel## Why This Stack- Matches preferred workflow- Fast enough for hackathon- Clean Vercel deployment- External DB works in production- Astro keeps shell lean- React islands handle just the interactive pieces## App FlowAstro page shell→ React app shell island→ user submits prompt/file→ Astro API `/api/transform`→ OpenAI Responses API→ structured JSON→ save session + input + output + events in Supabase→ render 4 panels one at a time## Required LLM BehaviorPromptr must:- classify prompt silently- choose one primary framework automatically- preserve strategic intent- reduce cognitive overload- separate human-safe prompt from machine-safe prompt- return structured JSON only## OpenAI Settings- Endpoint: Responses API- Model: gpt-5.2- Reasoning effort: medium- One model only for V1- Fallback env option later: gpt-5## Data Model### Table: sessionsTracks every anonymous visit.Columns:- id uuid primary key- session_token text unique not null- first_name text null- email text null- source text default 'web'- status text not null  - started  - submitted  - generated  - completed  - abandoned- created_at timestamptz default now()- updated_at timestamptz default now()- completed_at timestamptz null### Table: prompt_inputsStores original user prompt.Columns:- id uuid primary key- session_id uuid references sessions(id) on delete cascade- input_type text not null  - paste  - txt  - md  - docx- file_name text null- raw_prompt text not null- normalized_prompt text null- created_at timestamptz default now()### Table: prompt_outputsStores model result.Columns:- id uuid primary key- session_id uuid references sessions(id) on delete cascade- classification text not null- framework_used text not null- panel_1_activation_prompt text not null- panel_2_change_summary jsonb not null- panel_3_machine_layer text not null- panel_4_next_steps text not null- assumptions text null- model_name text not null- reasoning_level text not null- created_at timestamptz default now()### Table: panel_eventsTracks user movement and actions.Columns:- id uuid primary key- session_id uuid references sessions(id) on delete cascade- panel_name text not null  - intro  - input  - loading  - panel_1  - panel_2  - panel_3  - panel_4- event_type text not null  - viewed  - advanced  - backed  - copied  - downloaded_txt  - downloaded_md  - downloaded_pdf  - email_opened  - email_submitted- event_value text null- created_at timestamptz default now()### Table: launch_interestOptional clean capture table for email opt-in.Columns:- id uuid primary key- session_id uuid references sessions(id) on delete cascade- email text not null- created_at timestamptz default now()## Naming Conventions- Database: snake_case- App code: camelCase- Prompt file names: kebab-case- UI components: kebab-case file names, PascalCase component names- Shared constants in `/src/lib/constants.js`## Accepted Inputs- Pasted text- .txt- .md- .docx## Rejected Inputs- empty text- unreadable files- unsupported file types- PDFs- images- URLs## API Endpoints### POST /api/session/startCreates anonymous sessionInput:- firstName optionalOutput:- sessionToken- sessionId### POST /api/transformTransforms promptInput:- sessionToken- rawPrompt- inputType- fileName optionalOutput:- classification- frameworkUsed- assumptions- panel1ActivationPrompt- panel2WhatChanged- panel3MachineLayer- panel4UseThisNext### POST /api/eventsStores analytics eventsInput:- sessionToken- panelName- eventType- eventValue optional### POST /api/session/emailStores optional emailInput:- sessionToken- email## UI States- intro- input- loading- panel_1- panel_2- panel_3- panel_4## Visual Rules- Background: #050505- Card: #0f0f0f- Text: #fafafa- Muted: #9da4af- Bright accents restrained:  - #9b5cff  - #2de2e6  - #ff2f92  - optional #f97316- Fonts:  - Red Hat Display  - Red Hat Mono- Left-aligned text- Centered container- ~70% width desktop- ~75–80% max width mobile- Apple-like sleekness- Subtle glass + glow- Subtle motion only## Output Panel Rules### Panel 1- code-style block- ND-safe activation prompt- copy/download actions### Panel 2- short labeled sections- concise and blunt### Panel 3- collapsed by default- toggle line:  “Fuel for Promptr’s brain. Distracting AF for yours. Open if you’re curious.”### Panel 4- mini action plan- primary action = use the prompt- download actions- optional email toggle:  “Launch curious?”- reveal line:  “If you’ve got to know when Promptr’s ready for prime time...”- CTA:  “ADD ME”## Observability / GTM MetricsTrack:- session starts- prompt submitted- input type- classification- framework chosen- panel views- panel advances- back clicks- copies- downloads- email reveal- email submit- completion rate- dropout point## V1 Hard Guardrails- one model only- one transform call only- no edit mode- no branching maze- no extra dashboards- no feature creep
```

```
Build a polished micro web app called Promptr V1.Read every file in this project directory first before coding so you understand the product, visual direction, and workflow. Ask only one-part questions one at a time if something is truly blocking.Use this stack exactly:- Astro- React islands- JavaScript + JSX- Tailwind CSS- Lucide icons- Framer Motion- Supabase- OpenAI Responses API- Vercel deploymentDo not default to Next.js.Do not use TypeScript.Do not create a generic dashboard.Do not use default Tailwind blue.Do not center-align the copy.Do not add extra features that were not requested.Product:Promptr takes an overwhelming, multipart prompt and transforms it into:1. an ND-safe activation prompt2. a “what changed + why” explanation3. a machine-layer / bot-speak spec4. a short “use this next” action panelCore UX:- short branded intro screen first- then input screen- then premium loading screen- then 4-panel results flow- one panel at a time- Next / Back only- no visible progress counter- no visible loading barIntro screen:Headline:“Shift Your Prompt Results from Noise to Noice.”Support copy:“Remake nightmare mega-prompts.Smash cognitive overload.Get outputs you'll actually use.”Single CTA only.Input screen:Helper line:“Drop the prompt that breaks your brain here.”Formats:“Paste text or upload: .txt, .md, .docx”Use:- large textarea- left-aligned content- centered container- simple upload button with Lucide icon and caps labelLoading screen:- rotating short status lines- shuffled queue, no repeats until all phrases shown- typing cursor effect- subtle pulse- premium restrained motion- no progress barResults:Panel 1:- ND-safe activation prompt- code-style block- copy + export actionsPanel 2:- short labeled sections- concise, blunt, usefulPanel 3:- collapsed by default- line above toggle:  “Fuel for Promptr’s brain. Open if you’re curious.”Panel 4:- short action plan:  - copy the ND-safe version first  - run it in preferred LLM or agent  - save the ‘bot speak’ spec to build your own agent- export actions- hidden launch email toggle:  “Launch curious?”- reveal line:  “If you’ve got to know when Promptr’s ready for prime time...”- pill CTA:  “ADD ME”Backend:Use Astro API endpoints.Use Supabase as source of truth.Save every anonymous session automatically.No sign-in.Supported inputs:- pasted text- .txt- .md- .docxSupported outputs:- copy to clipboard- download TXT- download MD- download PDFModel:Use OpenAI Responses API with gpt-5.2.Use one model only for V1.Reasoning effort should start at medium.Require structured JSON output.Critical logic:Promptr must:- classify the prompt silently- auto-select one framework:  - FOG  - MVP  - SNAP  - PACE- default to PACE when multiple issues are present- preserve strategic intent- reduce human friction- separate human-safe prompt from machine-safe promptQuality bar:The app should feel polished, premium, and shippable.It should not feel like a hackathon toy.It should not feel cluttered.It should not over-help.Build output required:- complete file tree- working Astro project- API endpoints- Supabase SQL schema- env var list- local setup instructions- Vercel deploy instructions

## 4 — Promptr Agent Logic / Skills / Guardrails / Persona

JavaScript

```
// src/prompts/promptr-v1-system.jsexport const PROMPTR_V1_SYSTEM_PROMPT = `You are Promptr V1, an ND Prompt Refactor Architect.Your job:Transform an overwhelming, multipart, abandonment-prone prompt into a two-layer output system:1) a human-safe ND-friendly activation prompt2) a machine-safe backend prompt for stronger LLM executionAlso explain what changed and give the smallest next step so the user can actually use it.Core goal:Reduce cognitive overload without weakening strategic quality.Success criteria:- The user can understand and use the rewritten prompt without freezing.- The machine-layer prompt is stronger than the original.- The output is visibly better than the input.- The response feels sharp, useful, and human.Voice:- direct- smart- slightly rebellious- punchy- crisp- not corporate- not clinical- not motivational- not paddedHard style rules:- Do not use em dashes.- Do not over-explain.- Do not write long walls of text.- Do not sound like a therapist, professor, or generic copywriter.- Prefer short sections and crisp labels.- Prioritize clarity over cleverness.- Use sentence fragments when they hit harder.- Do not make the output more boring than the input.Assumptions:- The input may be messy, contradictory, incomplete, or emotionally overloaded.- Do not reject messy input.- Do not require perfect structure.- If needed, infer the most likely intent and proceed.- If a critical detail is missing, mention the assumption briefly in Panel 2.- Ask a clarifying question only if the prompt is impossible to salvage without it. If so, ask exactly one question and stop.Classify the prompt silently first into one of these:- writing- profile_or_bio- offer_or_sales- workflow_or_system- planning_or_strategy- agent_or_app_builder- intake_or_audit- mixed_or_otherFramework selection:Choose one primary framework only.Frameworks:- FOG = Friction -> Outcome -> GuardrailUse when the prompt is sprawling, undefined, or too broad.- MVP = Minimum Viable PermissionUse when perfectionism, fear, shame, or resistance is blocking action.- SNAP = State -> Next step -> Authority -> ProofUse when the user sounds stuck, flooded, avoidant, or needs a single next move.- PACE = Permission -> Anchor -> Containment -> ExecutionUse when both strategic complexity and cognitive overload are present.Default to PACE when multiple issues are present.Transformation rules:- Do not simply summarize the original prompt.- Do not lightly rewrite it and call it done.- Extract the actual task, desired outcome, hidden friction, and execution blockers.- Separate human friction from machine logic.- Turn blank-filling complexity into a smaller entry move.- Reduce decisions where possible.- Preserve strategic nuance where it matters.- Remove theatrics that do not improve output quality.- Keep enough specificity so the rewritten prompt still works.Output contract:Return valid JSON with exactly these keys:{  "classification": string,  "frameworkUsed": string,  "assumptions": string | null,  "panel1ActivationPrompt": string,  "panel2WhatChanged": {    "frameworkUsed": string,    "cut": string,    "clarified": string,    "rebuilt": string,    "whyItWorksBetter": string  },  "panel3MachineLayer": string,  "panel4UseThisNext": string}Panel requirements:Panel 1:- Human-usable version first- Easier to start- Less overwhelming- One clear path- Copy/paste readyPanel 2:- Brief- Blunt- Satisfying- Mention assumptions only if neededPanel 3:- Strong backend prompt- Clear role- Clear task- Constraints- Output format- Guardrails- Stronger than the originalPanel 4:- Tell the user to copy the ND-safe version first- Tell them to run it in their preferred LLM or agent- Mention they can save the bot-speak spec to build their own agent- Give one strongest next step only- Keep it shortGuardrails:- Do not shame the user.- Do not say the original prompt is bad.- Do not tell the user to calm down or try harder.- Do not replace sharp brand voice with generic professionalism.- Do not add fake specificity.- Do not over-compress so hard that the machine layer loses teeth.- If the prompt is clearly for a lead magnet, agent, or app, keep the output productizable.Final instruction:Extract the signal.Externalize the chaos.Make the damn thing usable.`.trim();
```

## 5 — Step-by-Step Sandbox Test Steps Before Final Production DB

Markdown

```
# Promptr V1 Sandbox Test Steps## GoalValidate:- model quality- JSON output shape- panel usefulness- file parsing- flow integritybefore fully wiring the production database.---## Step 1 — Create local envCreate `.env.local`Add:- OPENAI_API_KEY=- OPENAI_MODEL=gpt-5.2- NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL=- NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY=- SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY=If Supabase is not wired yet, stub session persistence temporarily.---## Step 2 — Build backend brain firstCreate:- `src/prompts/promptr-v1-system.js`- `src/pages/api/transform.js`- `src/lib/openai.js`Do not build the pretty UI first.Make the transform route work first.---## Step 3 — Terminal smoke test with pasted promptUse one real ugly mega-prompt.Example curl:```bashcurl -X POST http://localhost:4321/api/transform \  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \  -d '{    "sessionToken": "test-session-001",    "rawPrompt": "PASTE A REAL MESSY PROMPT HERE",    "inputType": "paste"  }'
```

Success looks like:

*   valid JSON only
    
*   all 4 panels returned
    
*   `frameworkUsed` populated
    
*   `classification` populated
    
*   panel 1 clearly different from panel 3
    

Failure looks like:

*   essay response
    
*   malformed JSON
    
*   panel 1 and panel 3 basically the same
    
*   panel 2 too long
    
*   panel 4 vague
    

* * *

## Step 4 — Prompt quality test

Run 3 different prompts:

1.  writing / offer prompt
    
2.  profile / bio prompt
    
3.  agent / app builder prompt
    

For each result, check:

### Panel 1

*   Is it actually easier to use?
    
*   Would an ND founder act on it?
    

### Panel 2

*   Is it short, sharp, and satisfying?
    

### Panel 3

*   Is it stronger than the original?
    
*   Does it preserve strategic bones?
    

### Panel 4

*   Is the next move obvious?
    
*   Is it short enough to act on immediately?
    

* * *

## Step 5 — File parser tests

Create:

*   one `.txt`
    
*   one `.md`
    
*   one `.docx`
    

Test that each extracts readable text.

Check:

*   formatting junk stripped
    
*   empty file handled gracefully
    
*   unsupported type rejected gracefully
    

* * *

## Step 6 — Build event logging stub

Before full Supabase wiring, at least log these in terminal or console:

*   session start
    
*   submit
    
*   panel view
    
*   panel advance
    
*   panel back
    
*   copy
    
*   download_txt
    
*   download_md
    
*   download_pdf
    
*   email_opened
    
*   email_submitted
    

Then swap to Supabase inserts.

* * *

## Step 7 — Wire Supabase schema

Create and run:

*   `supabase/schema.sql`
    

Then wire:

*   sessions
    
*   prompt_inputs
    
*   prompt_outputs
    
*   panel_events
    
*   launch_interest
    

Do this only after `/api/transform` is stable.

* * *

## Step 8 — Frontend shell build order

Build in this order:

1.  `src/pages/index.astro`
    
2.  `src/components/app-shell.jsx`
    
3.  `intro-screen.jsx`
    
4.  `prompt-input-screen.jsx`
    
5.  `loading-screen.jsx`
    
6.  `panel-shell.jsx`
    
7.  `result-panel-activation.jsx`
    
8.  `result-panel-changes.jsx`
    
9.  `result-panel-machine.jsx`
    
10.  `result-panel-next.jsx`
    

* * *

## Step 9 — UI behavior checks

Verify:

*   intro screen has one CTA only
    
*   input screen accepts paste and file upload
    
*   loading screen rotates phrases without obvious repeats
    
*   no progress bar
    
*   results move panel to panel cleanly
    
*   machine layer collapses by default
    
*   download buttons work
    
*   email toggle reveals correctly
    

Failure signs:

*   too much text on screen
    
*   clutter
    
*   default Tailwind look
    
*   copy centered
    
*   motion too twitchy
    
*   weak contrast
    

* * *

## Step 10 — Export tests

Verify all 4 work:

*   copy to clipboard
    
*   TXT download
    
*   MD download
    
*   PDF download
    

Check exported content matches on-screen content.

* * *

## Step 11 — Final local QA

Use 5 real prompts.  
Track:

*   average response time
    
*   any malformed JSON
    
*   any file parser failures
    
*   any panel that feels too long
    
*   any output that gets bland
    

Only after this should you fully trust the production DB wiring.

* * *

## Step 12 — Vercel deploy

Push repo to GitHub.  
Import into Vercel.  
Set env vars.  
Run production smoke test with:

*   paste input
    
*   docx input
    
*   email capture
    
*   download actions
    

If production behaves differently than local:

*   check API route runtime
    
*   check env var exposure
    
*   check CORS / server env
    
*   check Supabase service key usage

![](data:image/svg+xml;utf8,%3Csvg%20xmlns%3D%22http%3A%2F%2Fwww.w3.org%2F2000%2Fsvg%22%20viewBox%3D%220%200%2064%2064%22%20fill%3D%22none%22%3E%0A%20%20%3Crect%20width%3D%2264%22%20height%3D%2264%22%20rx%3D%2216%22%20fill%3D%22%23050505%22%3E%3C%2Frect%3E%0A%20%20%3Crect%20x%3D%228%22%20y%3D%228%22%20width%3D%2248%22%20height%3D%2248%22%20rx%3D%2214%22%20stroke%3D%22url(%23g)%22%20stroke-width%3D%221.5%22%3E%3C%2Frect%3E%0A%20%20%3Cpath%20d%3D%22M22%2024h20M22%2032h12M22%2040h16%22%20stroke%3D%22%23F3F4F6%22%20stroke-width%3D%222.5%22%20stroke-linecap%3D%22round%22%3E%3C%2Fpath%3E%0A%20%20%3Cdefs%3E%0A%20%20%20%20%3ClinearGradient%20id%3D%22g%22%20x1%3D%228%22%20y1%3D%228%22%20x2%3D%2256%22%20y2%3D%2256%22%20gradientUnits%3D%22userSpaceOnUse%22%3E%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%3Cstop%20stop-color%3D%22%23FF6164%22%3E%3C%2Fstop%3E%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%3Cstop%20offset%3D%220.33%22%20stop-color%3D%22%23FF8C42%22%3E%3C%2Fstop%3E%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%3Cstop%20offset%3D%220.66%22%20stop-color%3D%22%23BA0652%22%3E%3C%2Fstop%3E%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%3Cstop%20offset%3D%221%22%20stop-color%3D%22%238042F0%22%3E%3C%2Fstop%3E%0A%20%20%20%20%3C%2FlinearGradient%3E%0A%20%20%3C%2Fdefs%3E%0A%3C%2Fsvg%3E)

src/components/app-shell.jsx

JavaScript

```
import { useEffect, useMemo, useState } from "react";import IntroScreen from "./intro-screen";import PromptInputScreen from "./prompt-input-screen";import LoadingScreen from "./loading-screen";import PanelShell from "./panel-shell";import ResultPanelActivation from "./result-panel-activation";import ResultPanelChanges from "./result-panel-changes";import ResultPanelMachine from "./result-panel-machine";import ResultPanelNext from "./result-panel-next";import { trackEvent } from "../lib/analytics";import { buildFullExportPayload } from "../lib/utils";export default function AppShell() {  const [screen, setScreen] = useState("intro");  const [sessionToken, setSessionToken] = useState("");  const [sessionId, setSessionId] = useState("");  const [firstName, setFirstName] = useState("");  const [rawPrompt, setRawPrompt] = useState("");  const [results, setResults] = useState(null);  const [panelIndex, setPanelIndex] = useState(0);  const [error, setError] = useState("");  const [busy, setBusy] = useState(false);  const panelNames = ["panel_1", "panel_2", "panel_3", "panel_4"];  const exportPayload = useMemo(() => {    if (!results) return null;    return buildFullExportPayload(results);  }, [results]);  useEffect(() => {    if (!screen.startsWith("panel") || !sessionToken) return;    const panelName = panelNames[panelIndex];    trackEvent(sessionToken, panelName, "viewed").catch(() => {});  }, [screen, panelIndex, sessionToken]);  async function startAnonymousSession(name = "") {    const response = await fetch("/api/session/start", {      method: "POST",      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },      body: JSON.stringify({ firstName: name || null }),    });    if (!response.ok) {      throw new Error("Could not start session.");    }    const data = await response.json();    setSessionToken(data.sessionToken);    setSessionId(data.sessionId);    return data;  }  async function handleBegin() {    setError("");    setScreen("input");  }  async function handleSubmit({ promptText, firstNameValue }) {    if (!promptText?.trim()) {      setError("Drop the prompt that breaks your brain here first.");      return;    }    try {      setBusy(true);      setError("");      let currentToken = sessionToken;      if (!currentToken) {        const started = await startAnonymousSession(firstNameValue || firstName);        currentToken = started.sessionToken;      }      setFirstName(firstNameValue || firstName || "");      setRawPrompt(promptText);      setScreen("loading");      await trackEvent(currentToken, "input", "advanced", "submitted");      const response = await fetch("/api/transform", {        method: "POST",        headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },        body: JSON.stringify({          sessionToken: currentToken,          rawPrompt: promptText,          inputType: "paste",        }),      });      if (!response.ok) {        throw new Error("Promptr hit turbulence. Try again.");      }      const data = await response.json();      setResults(data);      setPanelIndex(0);      setScreen("panel");    } catch (err) {      setError(err.message || "Something broke.");      setScreen("input");    } finally {      setBusy(false);    }  }  function handleNext() {    if (panelIndex >= 3) return;    trackEvent(sessionToken, panelNames[panelIndex], "advanced").catch(() => {});    setPanelIndex((prev) => prev + 1);  }  function handleBack() {    if (panelIndex <= 0) return;    trackEvent(sessionToken, panelNames[panelIndex], "backed").catch(() => {});    setPanelIndex((prev) => prev - 1);  }  async function handleEmailSubmit(email) {    if (!email || !sessionToken) return;    await fetch("/api/session/email", {      method: "POST",      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },      body: JSON.stringify({ sessionToken, email }),    });    await trackEvent(sessionToken, "panel_4", "email_submitted", email);  }  const currentPanel = results    ? [        <ResultPanelActivation          key="panel1"          sessionToken={sessionToken}          activationPrompt={results.panel1ActivationPrompt}          exportPayload={exportPayload}        />,        <ResultPanelChanges          key="panel2"          changeSummary={results.panel2WhatChanged}          frameworkUsed={results.frameworkUsed}          assumptions={results.assumptions}          classification={results.classification}        />,        <ResultPanelMachine          key="panel3"          sessionToken={sessionToken}          machineLayer={results.panel3MachineLayer}        />,        <ResultPanelNext          key="panel4"          sessionToken={sessionToken}          activationPrompt={results.panel1ActivationPrompt}          machineLayer={results.panel3MachineLayer}          nextSteps={results.panel4UseThisNext}          exportPayload={exportPayload}          onSubmitEmail={handleEmailSubmit}        />,      ][panelIndex]    : null;  return (    <div className="min-h-screen bg-[var(--bg)] text-[var(--text-primary)]">      {screen === "intro" && <IntroScreen onBegin={handleBegin} />}      {screen === "input" && (        <PromptInputScreen          firstName={firstName}          setFirstName={setFirstName}          onSubmit={handleSubmit}          error={error}          busy={busy}        />      )}      {screen === "loading" && <LoadingScreen />}      {screen === "panel" && results && (        <PanelShell          onBack={panelIndex > 0 ? handleBack : null}          onNext={panelIndex < 3 ? handleNext : null}        >          {currentPanel}        </PanelShell>      )}    </div>  );}
```

src/components/prompt-input-screen.jsx

JavaScript

```
import { useState } from "react";import { motion } from "framer-motion";import Textarea from "./ui/textarea";import Input from "./ui/input";import UploadButton from "./upload-button";import Button from "./ui/button";import { parseSupportedFile } from "../lib/file-parser";export default function PromptInputScreen({  firstName,  setFirstName,  onSubmit,  error,  busy,}) {  const [promptText, setPromptText] = useState("");  const [fileName, setFileName] = useState("");  const [localError, setLocalError] = useState("");  async function handleFile(file) {    try {      setLocalError("");      const extracted = await parseSupportedFile(file);      setPromptText(extracted);      setFileName(file.name);    } catch (err) {      setLocalError(err.message || "Could not read that file.");    }  }  return (    <section className="flex min-h-screen items-center justify-center px-6 py-20">      <motion.div        initial={{ opacity: 0, y: 14 }}        animate={{ opacity: 1, y: 0 }}        transition={{ duration: 0.4, ease: "easeOut" }}        className="glass-card w-full max-w-[70rem] px-8 py-12 sm:px-12 md:px-14"      >        <div className="mx-auto w-full max-w-[54rem]">          <p className="kicker mb-5">INPUT</p>          <h2 className="mb-3 font-sans text-3xl font-extrabold tracking-tighter text-[var(--text-primary)] sm:text-4xl">            Drop the prompt that breaks your brain here.          </h2>          <p className="mb-8 font-mono text-sm uppercase tracking-[0.18em] text-[var(--text-secondary)]">            Paste text or upload: .txt, .md, .docx          </p>          <div className="mb-5 max-w-md">            <Input              value={firstName}              onChange={(e) => setFirstName(e.target.value)}              placeholder="FIRST NAME (OPTIONAL)"            />          </div>          <Textarea            value={promptText}            onChange={(e) => setPromptText(e.target.value)}            placeholder="Paste the bloated, blank-filling, brain-breaking mega-prompt here..."          />          <div className="mt-4 flex flex-wrap items-center gap-4">            <UploadButton onFileSelect={handleFile} />            {fileName ? (              <span className="font-mono text-xs uppercase tracking-[0.16em] text-[var(--text-secondary)]">                Loaded: {fileName}              </span>            ) : null}          </div>          {(error || localError) && (            <p className="mt-5 font-mono text-sm text-[#FF6164]">              {localError || error}            </p>          )}          <div className="mt-10">            <Button              onClick={() => onSubmit({ promptText, firstNameValue: firstName })}              disabled={busy}            >              {busy ? "PROMPTR AT WORK..." : "ND-IFY MY PROMPT"}            </Button>          </div>        </div>      </motion.div>    </section>  );}
```

src/components/loading-screen.jsx

JavaScript

```
import { useEffect, useMemo, useState } from "react";import { motion } from "framer-motion";import { STATUS_PHRASES } from "../lib/constants";import { shuffleArray } from "../lib/utils";export default function LoadingScreen() {  const [queue, setQueue] = useState([]);  const [phraseIndex, setPhraseIndex] = useState(0);  const [typed, setTyped] = useState("");  const [phase, setPhase] = useState("typing");  const phrases = useMemo(() => {    return shuffleArray([...STATUS_PHRASES]);  }, []);  useEffect(() => {    setQueue(phrases);  }, [phrases]);  useEffect(() => {    if (!queue.length) return;    const phrase = queue[phraseIndex % queue.length];    if (phase === "typing") {      if (typed.length < phrase.length) {        const timeout = setTimeout(() => {          setTyped(phrase.slice(0, typed.length + 1));        }, 28);        return () => clearTimeout(timeout);      }      const hold = setTimeout(() => setPhase("pulse"), 300);      return () => clearTimeout(hold);    }    if (phase === "pulse") {      const timeout = setTimeout(() => setPhase("clearing"), 1200);      return () => clearTimeout(timeout);    }    if (phase === "clearing") {      if (typed.length > 0) {        const timeout = setTimeout(() => {          setTyped((prev) => prev.slice(0, -1));        }, 18);        return () => clearTimeout(timeout);      }      const nextIndex = phraseIndex + 1;      if (nextIndex >= queue.length) {        setQueue(shuffleArray([...queue]));        setPhraseIndex(0);      } else {        setPhraseIndex(nextIndex);      }      setPhase("typing");    }  }, [typed, phase, queue, phraseIndex]);  return (    <section className="flex min-h-screen items-center justify-center px-6 py-20">      <div className="glass-card flex min-h-[20rem] w-full max-w-[70rem] items-center px-8 py-16 sm:px-12 md:px-16">        <div className="mx-auto w-full max-w-[54rem]">          <p className="kicker mb-5">ANALYZING</p>          <div className="min-h-[6rem] font-sans text-3xl font-extrabold tracking-tighter text-[var(--text-primary)] sm:text-4xl">            <motion.span              animate={phase === "pulse" ? { opacity: [1, 0.65, 1] } : { opacity: 1 }}              transition={{                duration: 0.9,                repeat: phase === "pulse" ? 2 : 0,                ease: "easeInOut",              }}            >              {typed}            </motion.span>            <span className="ml-1 inline-block animate-pulse text-[var(--accent-cyan)]">              _            </span>          </div>        </div>      </div>    </section>  );}
```

import { useState } from "react";import { Sparkles } from "lucide-react";import Button from "./ui/button";import DownloadActions from "./download-actions";import LaunchCuriousToggle from "./launch-curious-toggle";import { copyToClipboard } from "../lib/utils";import { trackEvent } from "../lib/analytics";export default function ResultPanelNext({  sessionToken,  activationPrompt,  nextSteps,  exportPayload,  onSubmitEmail,}) {  const [copied, setCopied] = useState(false);  async function handleCopy() {    await copyToClipboard(activationPrompt);    await trackEvent(sessionToken, "panel_4", "copied", "activation_prompt");    setCopied(true);    setTimeout(() => setCopied(false), 1800);  }  return (    <div>      <p className="kicker mb-4">USE THIS NEXT</p>      <h3 className="mb-6 font-sans text-3xl font-extrabold tracking-tighter text-[var(--text-primary)]">        Smallest next move wins.      </h3>      <div className="space-y-3 font-mono text-sm leading-7 text-[var(--text-primary)]">        <p>Copy the ND-safe version first.</p>        <p>Run it in your preferred LLM or agent.</p>        <p>Save the &lsquo;bot speak&rsquo; spec to build your own agent.</p>      </div>      <div className="mt-8">        <Button onClick={handleCopy}>          <Sparkles size={16} strokeWidth={1.75} />          {copied ? (        <div className="mt-5 max-w-xl space-y-4">          <p className="font-mono text-sm text-[var(--text-secondary)]">            If you&apos;ve got to know when Promptr&apos;s ready for prime time...          </p>          <div className="flex flex-col gap-3 sm:flex-row">            <Input              value={email}              onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}              placeholder="EMAIL ADDRESS"              type="email"            />            <Button onClick={handleSubmit} disabled={done}>              <BellPlus size={16} strokeWidth={1.75} />              {done ? "YOU'RE IN" : "ADD ME"}            </Button>          </div>        </div>      ) : null}    </div>  );}

"span" : "button";  return (    <Comp      type={asSpan ? undefined : type}      onClick={asSpan ? undefined : onClick}      disabled={asSpan ? undefined : disabled}      className={cn(        "group inline-flex items-center gap-2 rounded-full px-5 py-3 font-mono text-xs uppercase tracking-[0.22em] transition-all duration-300",        "focus:outline-none focus:ring-0",        variant === "primary" &&          "rainbow-outline text-[var(--text-primary)] hover:-translate-y-0.5",        variant === "secondary" &&          "border border-white/10 bg-white/[0.03] text-[var(--text-primary)] hover:-translate-y-0.5 hover:border-white/20 hover:bg-white/[0.05]",        disabled && "pointer-events-none opacity-50",        className      )}    >      {children}    </Comp>  );}

src/lib/analytics.js

JavaScript

```
export async function trackEvent(sessionToken, panelName, eventType, eventValue = null) {  if (!sessionToken) return;  try {    await fetch("/api/events", {      method: "POST",      headers: {        "Content-Type": "application/json",      },      body: JSON.stringify({        sessionToken,        panelName,        eventType,        eventValue,      }),    });  } catch (error) {    console.error("Event tracking failed:", error);  }}
```

```
export const APP_NAME = "Promptr V1";export const STATUS_PHRASES = [  "extracting the signal",  "sorting the strategic bones",  "stripping the friction",  "rewiring the entry point",  "separating human from bot speak",  "making the damn thing usable",  "taming the chaos",  "reducing cognitive drag",  "finding the clean next move",  "rebuilding for actual action",];

src/lib/file-parser.js

JavaScript

```
import mammoth from "mammoth/mammoth.browser";export async function parseSupportedFile(file) {  const ext = file.name.split(".").pop()?.toLowerCase();  if (!["txt", "md", "docx"].includes(ext)) {    throw new Error("Unsupported file type.");  }  if (ext === "txt" || ext === "md") {    return await file.text();  }  if (ext === "docx") {    const arrayBuffer = await file.arrayBuffer();    const result = await mammoth.extractRawText({ arrayBuffer });    return result.value?.trim() || "";  }  throw new Error("Could not parse file.");}
```

src/lib/openai.js

JavaScript

```
import OpenAI from "openai";import { PROMPTR_V1_SYSTEM_PROMPT } from "../prompts/promptr-v1-system.js";import { buildTransformUserPrompt } from "./prompt-builder.js";import { cleanJsonString, safeJsonParse } from "./utils.js";const client = new OpenAI({  apiKey: process.env.OPENAI_API_KEY,});export async function runPromptrTransform(rawPrompt) {  const response = await client.responses.create({    model: process.env.OPENAI_MODEL || "gpt-5.2",    reasoning: { effort: "medium" },    input: [      {        role: "system",        content: PROMPTR_V1_SYSTEM_PROMPT,      },      {        role: "user",        content: buildTransformUserPrompt(rawPrompt),      },    ],  });  const outputText = response.output_text || "";  const cleaned = cleanJsonString(outputText);  const parsed = safeJsonParse(cleaned);  if (!parsed) {    throw new Error("Model returned malformed JSON.");  }  return parsed;}
```

src/lib/pdf.js

JavaScript

```
import { jsPDF } from "jspdf";import { downloadTextFile } from "./utils";export function exportAsText(payload) {  downloadTextFile("promptr-output.txt", payload.plainText);}export function exportAsMarkdown(payload) {  downloadTextFile("promptr-output.md", payload.markdown);}export async function exportAsPdf(payload) {  const doc = new jsPDF({    unit: "pt",    format: "a4",  });  const left = 48;  let top = 56;  const pageWidth = doc.internal.pageSize.getWidth();  const maxWidth = pageWidth - left * 2;  const blocks = payload.plainText.split("\n\n");  doc.setFillColor(5, 5, 5);  doc.rect(0, 0, pageWidth, doc.internal.pageSize.getHeight(), "F");  doc.setFont("courier", "normal");  doc.setTextColor(243, 244, 246);  doc.setFontSize(10);  blocks.forEach((block) => {    const lines = doc.splitTextToSize(block, maxWidth);    if (top + lines.length * 14 > 760) {      doc.addPage();      doc.setFillColor(5, 5, 5);      doc.rect(0, 0, pageWidth, doc.internal.pageSize.getHeight(), "F");      doc.setFont("courier", "normal");      doc.setTextColor(243, 244, 246);      doc.setFontSize(10);      top = 56;    }    doc.text(lines, left, top);    top += lines.length * 14 + 20;  });  doc.save("promptr-output.pdf");}
```

import { createClient } from "@supabase/supabase-js";export function getSupabaseAdmin() {  return createClient(    process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL || process.env.PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL,    process.env.SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY,    {      auth: {        persistSession: false,        autoRefreshToken: false,      },    }  );}

src/lib/utils.js

```
export function cn(...classes) {  return classes.filter(Boolean).join(" ");}export function shuffleArray(array) {  const clone = [...array];  for (let i = clone.length - 1; i > 0; i -= 1) {    const j = Math.floor(Math.random() * (i + 1));    [clone[i], clone[j]] = [clone[j], clone[i]];  }  return clone;}export function cleanJsonString(value) {  return value    .replace(/^```json\s*/i, "")    .replace(/^```\s*/i, "")    .replace(/```$/i, "")    .trim();}export function safeJsonParse(value) {  try {    return JSON.parse(value);  } catch {    return null;  }}export async function copyToClipboard(value) {  await navigator.clipboard.writeText(value);}export function downloadTextFile(filename, content) {  const blob = new Blob([content], { type: "text/plain;charset=utf-8" });  const url = URL.createObjectURL(blob);  const anchor = document.createElement("a");  anchor.href = url;  anchor.download = filename;  anchor.click();  URL.revokeObjectURL(url);}export function buildFullExportPayload(results) {  const markdown = `# ND-SAFE ACTIVATION PROMPT\`\`\`${results.panel1ActivationPrompt}\`\`\`# WHAT CHANGED + WHY- Framework used: ${results.panel2WhatChanged.frameworkUsed}- Cut: ${results.panel2WhatChanged.cut}- Clarified: ${results.panel2WhatChanged.clarified}- Rebuilt: ${results.panel2WhatChanged.rebuilt}- Why it works better: ${results.panel2WhatChanged.whyItWorksBetter}${results.assumptions ? `- Assumptions: ${results.assumptions}` : ""}# MACHINE LAYER / BOT SPEAK SPEC\`\`\`${results.panel3MachineLayer}\`\`\`# USE THIS NEXT${results.panel4UseThisNext}`;  const plainText = `ND-SAFE ACTIVATION PROMPT${results.panel1ActivationPrompt}WHAT CHANGED + WHYFramework used: ${results.panel2WhatChanged.frameworkUsed}Cut: ${results.panel2WhatChanged.cut}Clarified: ${results.panel2WhatChanged.clarified}Rebuilt: ${results.panel2WhatChanged.rebuilt}Why it works better: ${results.panel2WhatChanged.whyItWorksBetter}${results.assumptions ? `Assumptions: ${results.assumptions}\n` : ""}MACHINE LAYER / BOT SPEAK SPEC${results.panel3MachineLayer}USE THIS NEXT${results.panel4UseThisNext}`;  return { markdown, plainText };}

src/pages/api/events.js

JavaScript

```
import { getSupabaseAdmin } from "../../lib/supabase.js";export async function POST({ request }) {  try {    const { sessionToken, panelName, eventType, eventValue = null } = await request.json();    const supabase = getSupabaseAdmin();    const { data: session } = await supabase      .from("sessions")      .select("id")      .eq("session_token", sessionToken)      .single();    if (!session) {      return new Response(JSON.stringify({ ok: false }), { status: 404 });    }    await supabase.from("panel_events").insert({      session_id: session.id,      panel_name: panelName,      event_type: eventType,      event_value: eventValue,    });    return new Response(JSON.stringify({ ok: true }), {      status: 200,      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },    });  } catch (error) {    return new Response(JSON.stringify({ ok: false, error: error.message }), {      status: 500,      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },    });  }}
```

src/pages/api/transform.js

JavaScript

```
import { getSupabaseAdmin } from "../../lib/supabase.js";import { runPromptrTransform } from "../../lib/openai.js";export async function POST({ request }) {  try {    const { sessionToken, rawPrompt, inputType = "paste", fileName = null } = await request.json();    if (!rawPrompt || rawPrompt.trim().length < 40) {      return new Response(        JSON.stringify({ error: "Prompt is too short to ND-ify properly." }),        {          status: 400,          headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },        }      );    }    const supabase = getSupabaseAdmin();    const { data: session } = await supabase      .from("sessions")      .select("id")      .eq("session_token", sessionToken)      .single();    if (!session) {      return new Response(JSON.stringify({ error: "Session not found." }), {        status: 404,        headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },      });    }    await supabase.from("prompt_inputs").insert({      session_id: session.id,      input_type: inputType,      file_name: fileName,      raw_prompt: rawPrompt,      normalized_prompt: rawPrompt.trim(),    });    await supabase      .from("sessions")      .update({ status: "submitted", updated_at: new Date().toISOString() })      .eq("id", session.id);    const transformed = await runPromptrTransform(rawPrompt);    await supabase.from("prompt_outputs").insert({      session_id: session.id,      classification: transformed.classification,      framework_used: transformed.frameworkUsed,      panel_1_activation_prompt: transformed.panel1ActivationPrompt,      panel_2_change_summary: transformed.panel2WhatChanged,      panel_3_machine_layer: transformed.panel3MachineLayer,      panel_4_next_steps: transformed.panel4UseThisNext,      assumptions: transformed.assumptions,      model_name: process.env.OPENAI_MODEL || "gpt-5.2",      reasoning_level: "medium",    });    await supabase      .from("sessions")      .update({ status: "generated", updated_at: new Date().toISOString() })      .eq("id", session.id);    return new Response(      JSON.stringify({        classification: transformed.classification,        frameworkUsed: transformed.frameworkUsed,        assumptions: transformed.assumptions,        panel1ActivationPrompt: transformed.panel1ActivationPrompt,        panel2WhatChanged: transformed.panel2WhatChanged,        panel3MachineLayer: transformed.panel3MachineLayer,        panel4UseThisNext: transformed.panel4UseThisNext,      }),      {        status: 200,        headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },      }    );  } catch (error) {    return new Response(JSON.stringify({ error: error.message }), {      status: 500,      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },    });  }}
```

src/pages/api/session/email.js

JavaScript

```
import { getSupabaseAdmin } from "../../../lib/supabase.js";export async function POST({ request }) {  try {    const { sessionToken, email } = await request.json();    if (!email) {      return new Response(JSON.stringify({ error: "Email required." }), {        status: 400,        headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },      });    }    const supabase = getSupabaseAdmin();    const { data: session } = await supabase      .from("sessions")      .select("id")      .eq("session_token", sessionToken)      .single();    if (!session) {      return new Response(JSON.stringify({ error: "Session not found." }), {        status: 404,        headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },      });    }    await supabase.from("launch_interest").insert({      session_id: session.id,      email,    });    await supabase      .from("sessions")      .update({ email, updated_at: new Date().toISOString() })      .eq("id", session.id);    return new Response(JSON.stringify({ ok: true }), {      status: 200,      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },    });  } catch (error) {    return new Response(JSON.stringify({ error: error.message }), {      status: 500,      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },    });  }}
```

src/pages/api/session/start.js

JavaScript

```
import { getSupabaseAdmin } from "../../../lib/supabase.js";export async function POST({ request }) {  try {    const { firstName = null } = await request.json();    const sessionToken = crypto.randomUUID();    const supabase = getSupabaseAdmin();    const { data, error } = await supabase      .from("sessions")      .insert({        session_token: sessionToken,        first_name: firstName,        status: "started",      })      .select("id")      .single();    if (error) {      throw error;    }    return new Response(      JSON.stringify({        sessionToken,        sessionId: data.id,      }),      {        status: 200,        headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },      }    );  } catch (error) {    return new Response(JSON.stringify({ error: error.message }), {      status: 500,      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },    });  }}
```

supabase/schema.sql

SQL

```
create extension if not exists "pgcrypto";create table if not exists sessions (  id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),  session_token text unique not null,  first_name text,  email text,  source text not null default 'web',  status text not null,  created_at timestamptz not null default now(),  updated_at timestamptz not null default now(),  completed_at timestamptz);create table if not exists prompt_inputs (  id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),  session_id uuid not null references sessions(id) on delete cascade,  input_type text not null,  file_name text,  raw_prompt text not null,  normalized_prompt text,  created_at timestamptz not null default now());create table if not exists prompt_outputs (  id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),  session_id uuid not null references sessions(id) on delete cascade,  classification text not null,  framework_used text not null,  panel_1_activation_prompt text not null,  panel_2_change_summary jsonb not null,  panel_3_machine_layer text not null,  panel_4_next_steps text not null,  assumptions text,  model_name text not null,  reasoning_level text not null,  created_at timestamptz not null default now());create table if not exists panel_events (  id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),  session_id uuid not null references sessions(id) on delete cascade,  panel_name text not null,  event_type text not null,  event_value text,  created_at timestamptz not null default now());create table if not exists launch_interest (  id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),  session_id uuid not null references sessions(id) on delete cascade,  email text not null,  created_at timestamptz not null default now());create index if not exists idx_sessions_token on sessions(session_token);create index if not exists idx_prompt_inputs_session on prompt_inputs(session_id);create index if not exists idx_prompt_outputs_session on prompt_outputs(session_id);create index if not exists idx_panel_events_session on panel_events(session_id);create index if not exists idx_launch_interest_session on launch_interest(session_id);
```

## Q: 
Okay, so now just to verify, the 'build' prompt I was going to feed to Antigravity is not really a necessary thing, per se, is it? Instead, they'll act as my code check / diagnosis and tell me what they need for me to set up in human speak to get the front end and the backend connected, is that right?

## A: 
Right. At this point, the big **build prompt** is no longer the main thing.

Because now you already have:

*   the product logic
    
*   the file tree
    
*   the system prompt
    
*   the schema
    
*   the frontend files
    
*   the backend files
    

So Antigravity’s job shifts from **“invent the app”** to:

**assemble, sanity-check, wire, debug, and deploy the app you already specified.**

## So the clean answer is:

**No, the giant build prompt is not strictly necessary anymore.**

What _is_ useful now is a **much shorter Antigravity instruction** that says, in human speak:

*   review the provided files
    
*   verify what’s missing or broken
    
*   tell me exactly what I need to set up
    
*   connect frontend ↔ API ↔ Supabase ↔ OpenAI
    
*   explain blockers in non-dev language
    
*   test locally before deploy
    

## Use this with Antigravity now

```
Review all files in this Promptr V1 project first before changing anything.Your job is no longer to invent the app. Your job is to:1. verify the file structure and code are coherent2. identify anything missing, broken, inconsistent, or risky3. tell me in plain English what I need to set up next to connect:   - frontend   - Astro API endpoints   - Supabase   - OpenAI4. make the minimum necessary fixes to get the app working locally5. test the app in the terminal and report what passed, what failed, and what still needs setup from me6. keep all explanations in non-developer speak unless code is requiredImportant:- do not rewrite the product- do not change the UX direction unless something is functionally broken- do not add extra features- do not drift from Astro + React islands + JS- if something is unclear, ask me one question at a timeAssume I want the fastest path to:working local demo → verified backend connections → Vercel deploy
```

## What AG should help you identify next

In plain English, they should tell you things like:

*   whether your `package.json` dependencies are enough
    
*   whether Astro API routes are wired correctly
    
*   whether the OpenAI call shape works as written
    
*   whether Supabase env vars are named correctly
    
*   whether the DB schema matches the inserts
    
*   whether the frontend components actually connect to the backend
    
*   what you personally need to create in Supabase
    
*   what you personally need to paste into `.env.local`
    

## So your workflow now is:

**You:** paste in the files  
**AG:** checks, wires, tests, explains setup gaps  
**You:** supply keys / Supabase project / env vars  
**AG:** fixes remaining issues and gets it running

That’s the correct split now.

If you want, the next thing I’d help you with is a **human checklist of what _you_ need to set up outside the code** before AG can run the app.

## Q: 
Give me your version of what I need to set up, sure. Make it a checklist. Easy steps, non-dev stuff. I'm about out of time now

## A: 
Here’s your **non-dev, do-this-now checklist** so AG can wire and test Promptr without you burning another hour decoding setup crap.

# Promptr V1 Setup Checklist

## 1) Create your Supabase project

*    Log into Supabase
    
*    Create a **new project**
    
*    Name it something obvious like `promptr-v1`
    
*    Save the database password somewhere you won’t lose it
    

## 2) Grab your Supabase keys

Inside your Supabase project:

*    Copy the **Project URL**
    
*    Copy the **Anon/Public Key**
    
*    Copy the **Service Role Key**
    

These go into your `.env.local` file later.

## 3) Create your OpenAI API key

*    Log into your OpenAI platform account
    
*    Create a new **API key**
    
*    Save it somewhere safe
    
*    Make sure billing is turned on enough for demo calls
    

## 4) Make sure your local project folder is clean

*    Delete the old broken/restarted project folder if needed
    
*    Create a fresh `promptr-v1` project folder on your external drive
    
*    Paste in all the files exactly where they belong
    

## 5) Create the env file

In the root of the project:

*    Make a file called `.env.local`
    
*    Add these values:
    

env

```
OPENAI_API_KEY=your_openai_key_hereOPENAI_MODEL=gpt-5.2PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL=your_supabase_project_url_herePUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY=your_supabase_anon_key_hereSUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY=your_supabase_service_role_key_here
```

## 6) Run the database schema

In Supabase:

*    Open the **SQL Editor**
    
*    Paste in the contents of `supabase/schema.sql`
    
*    Run it
    
*    Confirm the tables were created
    

You should see:

*    `sessions`
    
*    `prompt_inputs`
    
*    `prompt_outputs`
    
*    `panel_events`
    
*    `launch_interest`
    

## 7) Open the project in Antigravity

*    Point AG at the fresh project folder
    
*    Tell it to review the files first
    
*    Use the shorter AG instruction prompt, not the giant build brief
    

## 8) Have AG install dependencies

*    Let AG run the install command
    
*    Let AG tell you if any package is missing or wrong
    

## 9) Ask AG to do local testing first

*    Confirm the app starts locally
    
*    Confirm the API route works
    
*    Confirm Supabase connects
    
*    Confirm OpenAI connects
    
*    Confirm one real mega-prompt returns all 4 panels
    

## 10) Only after local works, set up GitHub

*    Create a new GitHub repo
    
*    Push the working local version there
    

## 11) Then set up Vercel

*    Import the GitHub repo into Vercel
    
*    Add the same env vars in Vercel
    
*    Deploy
    
*    Smoke test the live URL
    

# What you should NOT do right now

*    Don’t redesign anything
    
*    Don’t add more features
    
*    Don’t switch stacks again
    
*    Don’t start V2
    
*    Don’t obsess over polish before local works
    

# Fastest success path

1.  Supabase project
    
2.  OpenAI key
    
3.  `.env.local`
    
4.  run schema
    
5.  AG reviews files
    
6.  AG gets local demo working
    
7.  GitHub
    
8.  Vercel
    

If you want, next I’ll turn this into a **copy-paste note for Notion** with tighter formatting.

## Q: 
Would these be called: Publishable Key Secret Key

## A: 
Yes — **those are the new names you’ll often see now** for Supabase keys.

For your setup, the mapping is:

*   **Publishable Key** → use this for  
    `PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY`
    
*   **Secret Key** → use this for  
    `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`
    

That matches Supabase’s current guidance: publishable keys are safe for public/client use, and secret keys are for backend/server use only. Supabase also notes the older `anon` and `service_role` JWT keys are legacy and the new publishable/secret keys are preferred.   [Supabase](https://supabase.com/docs/guides/api/api-keys)  

So in practical terms for your `.env.local`, you can do:

env

```
PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL=your_project_urlPUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY=your_publishable_keySUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY=your_secret_key
```

One important thing: **never expose the Secret Key in the browser.** It belongs server-side only. Supabase explicitly warns secret/service-role keys have elevated access and must not be exposed publicly.   [Supabase](https://supabase.com/docs/guides/api/api-keys)

## Q: 
Okay, and do I need to add the name/label in the env file since I named it Promptr_V1 or no?

## A: 
No. You **do not** put your project name label in the env variable names.

The env file should use the **exact variable names the code expects**, not whatever you named the Supabase project in the dashboard.

So keep it like this:

env

```
OPENAI_API_KEY=your_openai_key_hereOPENAI_MODEL=gpt-5.2PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL=your_supabase_project_url_herePUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY=your_publishable_key_hereSUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY=your_secret_key_here
```

Your Supabase project can be named **Promptr_V1** in the dashboard. That’s fine.  
But the env labels stay generic unless the code itself is written to look for custom names.

So: **project name = no**  
**exact env var names = yes**
